< Text>
I'm leaving my intial review, because I think my updated review will have more impact this way. I was until last night a regular at this place for the past 6 months, since I found it after finding 45 minute waits at my regular places and was too hungry to wait. I loved this place. I told everyone about it. But what a difference a day can make. They refused me service. Yes, really. I showed up at 8:45 and the place was not busy on a Friday. They had  most tables open. I asked to be seated and they showed me a table in the middle, I did not like because it was in front of the door. I asked for the table in the back-side. The Hostess/waitress/manger/whoever, then told me they close at 9 and they aren't seating anymore tables. They actually close at 10. I've been there late, probably after 10. I accepted their decision and had a pleasant meal at Road To Soul.  I can't keep up a 5 Star rating for a restaurant that refused me service so now it's a 1 star and the friend I was with gave them 1 star, on Yelp. I am so personally hurt by this experience. A great restaurant has fallen.
This Old Review no longer true: "Amazing Bon-Chon. Great value. Good food. All this for $52.00 American. Friendly staff."<//Text>

< Text>
A nice casual spot to grab some delicious Boudin. Just try to arrive a little bit early or late otherwise you'll encounter a wait in line that usually runs out the door. Calling your order ahead might help but the food usually comes out so quickly (and fresh) that it usually won't  make much of a difference.

Nice comfortable quiet seating in the back and patio seating. As always great Boudin food for the middle of your day working downtown.< /Text>

<user_name>Sukhraj Beasla (Suki)<//user_name><Time>1396046887033</Time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
<Review>The smell of fresh baked bread will tempt you and if that isn't enough they put on a window show so you can watch as they prepare their yummy goodness live and send out samples. That was enough for us to walk in and sit down for lunch.

The wait was 20 minutes so we took a tour of the gift shop and then headed upstairs where we noticed there was a museum tour for $3 however we watched from above as the flour is brought in on an assembly line, dumped into a large vat, mixed with eggs, water, etc, and then prepared into bread. That was pretty neat and made the wait time go by fast.

We got a lovely window seat next to a couple from the East coast and watched street traffic while waiting for service. We also learned that everyone around us was here to run the race including our waiter. Go figure.

I ordered the chicken club sandwich with shoe string fries. The order was prompt but we never got our complimentary bread until the end of the meal. Oh well. The sandwich itself had a juicy chicken breast, crisp bacon, ripe pieces of avocado, and crisp romaine lettuce. It was so unbelievably yummy. After having walked up and down Fisherman's Wharf, I was starving so I ate my sandwich and half of my fries in about 15 minutes and before the waiter could come back and check up on us.

I also loved that during the race Boudin was handing out bread. They were at mile 1 with bread baskets. I grabbed a few handfuls and ate them during my marathon. That was awesome!< /Review><pictures>None< /pictures><Response>None</Response><GmapID>0x80858088b64f1dc7:0xa1636c7ad1d9410f< /GmapID></record>

< text>
We're becoming regulars. First tried Kombucha here and now we are making it ourselves! Our favorites are the spinach cakes (appetizer), pesto pasta (hubby), beet salad (wifey) and sweet chili tofu on brown rice or in a wrap. A friend recommended the yam soup, but it was too spicy, even for me. However, I love the fact that I can get a roasted yam dinner or surf and turf (fish and portabello mushroom).
Its an old house and that's what makes for a very good atmosphere. Acoustics are bad, so don't talk above a whisper about anything personal; everyone will hear your business.
I love the vegan menu options, but would really like to see a calorie breakdown of the menu items.
They often forget to bring something you order, or get something mixed up first time, so be flexible. This is not a restaurant for people in a hurry; but the California whole foodies will feel right at home here.</text>

<Review>Twin Oaks Golf Course has made a real resurgence in the last 2 or 3 years. The greens are in incredible shape, and the fairways in many areas are lush and green, with a few patches of dead and muddy ground. Still, this course is an incredible value when you play twilight for $30 w/ a cart.

The putting green is a bit patchy around it, and it could use a larger area with more undulation to it.

I did not have the opportunity to use the driving range.

So why am I rating it a 1 star? In truth, if that was the whole story, I would have rated this somewhere between 3 and 4. However, the day I went there was a Junior Golf event happening. We showed up about 15min before our tee time only to find out they were "running a bit behind". Hmm, would be pushing it to finish before dark, but maybe we could get ~16 holes in? Ended up teeing off almost 40 min after our scheduled tee time. Brutal but could still get ~14 holes in? Not a chance. Every shot we had to wait 5-10 min. At the 8th hole the group in front of us decided to cut across and play holes 4-6 again. We figured this would be great and we would be moving faster, only to find that we ended up waiting behind 2 foursomes on #9 tee box. By the time we tee'd off the GPS in the cart said we had an elapsed 2:45min and were 45min behind pace.

The course was painfully slow. We would often pull up to a tee where the foursome 2 groups ahead was just getting ready to tee off.

I was kind of livid and disappointed. It felt like a waste of my time. I went into the pro shop to ask about this and was told they had 80 juniors on the course. I am not sure I see the relevance of that. If they had that many people, why were they selling tee times? Why not just shut the course down? Why not have a marshal to encourage the juniors to play faster? If I had known the pace of play was going to be that slow, I would have booked a time elsewhere.

The person at the pro shop offered me a voucher for 9 holes. I said no thanks, I wouldn't be using it. I have no intention of going back to this course. Spending 3 hours to play 9 holes is absurd, and they are doing those juniors a disservice allowing them to play that slowly. I can *walk* 18 holes at my home course (~7k yards) in 3 hours. Twin Oaks showed a lack of appreciation for my time, and my time is very valuable to me. What's worse is they didn't really make an effort to make it right.</Review>< user_name>
Ryan McCullough< /user_name>

< Text>
Honestly to say that this garden has many more elements than majority of the US parks. Koi, Ducks, Goose; Lake, Lawn, Bridges, Trees, Hills; also of course some Japanese style building. The garden size is relatively small, but it is really colorful. It is a great place to take some great photos! Kelly Park is just steps away and if you have more than 1 hour to spend...<//Text>

< Name>
Toshinobu Kubota< /Name>
<Date>1606697882850< /Date>< review>
Relaxing and pretty place for families of all sorts to come and enjoy. This park is from San Jose's sister city, Okayama-Shi, located in Japan, and everything in here preserves the Japanese serenity and traditional beauty.
What's not beautiful are some Instagram girls and wannabes who come here and hog the small walkways so they can take 470 pictures of themselves under the changing leaves.
Insider tip, parking and entrance are free during Covid, so there are plenty of people visiting this place. The best autumn leaves Kodak moments were between Nov 19-26. Don't forget to walk around the surrounding park and Happy Hallow if you have the time.<//review>

I am a Japanese enthusiast and was very excited to visit the garden. We came all the way from DC and were surprised to see the lake dry and the koi fish was in a small dirty pond you cannot even see them. The experience was extremely disappointing. On another note the staff were really friendly.<//text>

Was once a beautiful Oasis in a concrete city but now it's luscious koi-filled ponds are dry and people are rudely walking in them despite the clear signs not to. I visited this place after seeing some photos in Google maps. But it was not updated about the repair of large ponds. they were under repair and water was removed. the fish were removed to upper ponds. Anyhow a beautiful and attractive place with Japanese landscape. Many Japanese have come with their kids.

< Text>
The Japanese Friendship Garden
with its diverse landscapes, tall
trees and comforting grass areas
invites young and old families to
relax and explore. Some families set up easy tents just for the day.
Restrooms and tables are open,
BBQs are not.
You will see; birds, turtles, coy, and
and so much more. Amazing
japanese landscapes in San Jose?
Yes it is vivid and true. Visit once
and you will never forget what has
been experienced. Awesome, clean
and very friendly. There is a
peaceful resident crane that moves
elegantly and will fill you with
wonder. Leave a dollar or more in
donation "fountain".<//Text>

<user_id>103742819485008958293<//user_id>< review>
This was once one of my favorite places to visit in San Jose. At one time I would even argue that this was a better place to visit than the one in SF. At this point though it's not really worth even stopping at. Two thirds of the ponds have been dry for years. Yes, I understand this was a result of the sewage flood thanks to San Jose not being able to handle a little rain. I also understand this area wastes money on plenty of things that aren't as important to me, and we are talking several years now.

As bad as all that is, today was the final straw  At some point they taped a sign over their hours to close at 4PM. We didn't realize it until the ranger locked my girlfriend and I in. Some shouted, be we weren't able to understand exactly what was said.  We started walking to the gate to see what was going on, instead we only found it locked. In our escape planning we ran into another couple that was trapped as well.  I guess luckily for all of us the fence is in a similar state of disrepair to the ponds since we were a le to find a bald spot in the barbed wire to make a break for it.</review>

<rate>5< /rate>< review>
Beautiful and serene.  A gift from the city of Okayama in Japan during the early 60s.   A rare gem in San Jose, 6.5 acres and you will be transported to a thoughtful place where you are encouraged to be in the moment and relax.  Although the City is repairing the ponds from the flood 2.5 years ago still, the garden is still a haven for animals and beauty.  No fee to enter, parking is about $6 in Senter/Alma lot, and $10 in the lot next to Happy Hollow, free parking if you drive around the stadium area if it's not crowded.  Hours are generally 10am to 5pm, but maybe later - check the website.<//review>

<username>Jayasimha Nuggehalli<//username><Time>1574399257232<//Time><rate>5</rate>< Review>
This Japanese Garden is in Kelly Park San Jose. Park is around 6 acres, established in 1965` Entrance to the park is free. However there is a $10 fee for parking. You can also find free street parking near by. Great location for photo shoots or just relax in the garden. Garden has three ponds. Pond under the bridge is Koi pond.

This garden got affected by flood in San Jose, couple of years ago. Now restoration is going on in the garden specially Koi pond. Now the Koi pond is dry, Koi fish are moved to another pond in the garden. Now fund raising in progress to restore the garden.

In spite of this it is still a nice place to visit in San Jose.<//Review>

< Review>
Nicely maintained set of formal Japanese Gardens, with lots of fish to spot and little streams to walk over.  Lots of shade to stay out of the sun if you want to, but plenty of places to bask [if you feel like risking the wrath of the Geese - in October!].

The only downside for me, was that the obviously constructed nature of the Gardens was pretty obvious (concrete channels, edging etc) and this detracted somewhat from the 'natural' experience.</Review>

None< /Resp>
< text>
Saw big and little koi fish today.  Koi fish food available for a quarter from a machine -- don't feed them anything else!  Lovely park for watching water running and taking in the serene design.

But no picnicking allowed within this park.  You have to go outside and there are plenty of grass and picnic tables right behind this park.  Signs say to keep off grass, which is a bit sad given this is a park.  Might be a hassle with little ones as they just run anywhere.

Unfortunately the beautiful design is marred by cheap looking chain fences on the perimeter.<//text>
